# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Symptom observed in: path/to/symptom.ext
2. Called from: path/to/caller.ext (function name)
3. Bug triggered by: path/to/buggy.ext (function name, line ~N)
...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

## Analysis
[Detailed trace from symptom to root cause, explaining each step]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

66-assistanttext-
Perfect! The solution document is complete and comprehensive. Let me create a summary of what was found:

## Summary

I've completed a thorough investigation of the Kubernetes scheduler bug where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created.

### Key Findings:

**Root Causes Identified:**

1. **Missing GVK Constant** - `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 96)
   - `framework.ResourceSlice` is not defined in the GVK constants block

2. **Missing Event Registration** - `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 410)
   - The DynamicResources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method doesn't include ResourceSlice events

3. **Missing Event Handler** - `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (line 492)
   - No case handler for ResourceSlice in the `addAllEventHandlers()` switch statement

### Why This Is a Bug:

The scheduler uses **event-driven re-queuing** to move pods from the unschedulable queue back to active queue when cluster state changes. When a pod requests DRA resources:

1. If ResourceSlices don't exist when the pod arrives → scheduling fails
2. Pod is added to unschedulable queue
3. When ResourceSlices are later created → **no event handler triggers re-queuing**
4. Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever

### Proposed Fix:

Three coordinated changes:

1. Add `ResourceSlice GVK = "ResourceSlice"` constant to `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
2. Register ResourceSlice events in the DynamicResources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method
3. Add a case handler for ResourceSlice in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`

The complete analysis with detailed code diffs and traced execution path has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

\\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n236: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n237: \t\t}\n238: \n239: \t\tif runPermitStatus.IsRejected() {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \\tcntOfMaxScore := 1\\n871: \\tselectedIndex := 0\\n872: \\t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\\n873: \\tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \\n258: func statusForClaim(schedulingCtx *resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext, podClaimName string) *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaimSchedulingStatus {\\n259: \\tif schedulingCtx == nil {\\n260: \\t\\treturn nil\\n261: \\t}\\n262: \\tfor _, status := range schedulingCtx.Status.ResourceClaims {\\n263: \\t\\tif status.Name == podClaimName {\\n264: \\t\\t\\treturn &status\\n265: \\t\\t}\\n266: \\t}\\n267: \\treturn nil\\n268: }\\n269: \\n270: // dynamicResources is a plugin that ensures that ResourceClaims are allocated.\\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\\n272: \\tenabled                    bool\\n273: \\tfh                         framework.Handle\\n274: \\tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\\n275: \\tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\\n276: \\tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\\n277: \\tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\\n278: \\tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\\n279: \\tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\\n280: \\tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\\n281: \\tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\\n282: \\n283: \\t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\\n284: \\t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\\n285: \\t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\\n286: \\t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\\n287: \\t// the informer callback (based on the \\\"newer than\\\" comparison in the\\n288: \\t// assume cache).\\n289: \\t//\\n290: \\t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\\n291: \\t// therefore are \\\"<namespace>/<name>\\\".\\n292: \\t//\\n293: \\t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\\n294: \\t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\\n295: \\t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\\n296: \\t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\\n297: \\t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\\n298: \\t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\\n299: \\t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\\n300: \\t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\\n301: \\t//\\n302: \\t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\\n303: \\t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\\n304: \\t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\\n305: \\tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\\n306: \\n307: \\t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\\n308: \\t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\\n309: \\t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\\n310: \\t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \\\"not\\n311: \\t// schedulable yet\\\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\\n312: \\t// make it schedulable.\\n313: \\t//\\n314: \\t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\\n315: \\t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\\n316: \\t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\\n317: \\t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\\n318: \\t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\\n319: \\t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\\n320: \\t//\\n321: \\t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\\n322: \\t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\\n323: \\t// problem:\\n324: \\t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\\n325: \\t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\\n326: \\t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\\n327: \\t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\\n328: \\t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\\n329: \\t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\\n330: \\t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\\n331: \\t//\\n332: \\t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\\n333: \\t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\\n334: \\t// hitting the \\\"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\\n335: \\t// for disjoint sets of keys\\\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\\n336: \\tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\\n337: }\\n338: allocated.\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\n272: \tenabled                    bool\n273: \tfh                         framework.Handle\n274: \tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\n275: \tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\n276: \tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\n277: \tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\n278: \tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\n279: \tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\n280: \tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\n281: \tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\n282: \n283: \t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\n284: \t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\n285: \t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\n286: \t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\n287: \t// the informer callback (based on the \"newer than\" comparison in the\n288: \t// assume cache).\n289: \t//\n290: \t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\n291: \t// therefore are \"<namespace>/<name>\".\n292: \t//\n293: \t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\n294: \t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\n295: \t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\n296: \t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\n297: \t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\n298: \t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\n299: \t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\n300: \t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\n301: \t//\n302: \t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\n303: \t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\n304: \t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\n305: \tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\n306: \n307: \t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\n308: \t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\n309: \t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\n310: \t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \"not\n311: \t// schedulable yet\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\n312: \t// make it schedulable.\n313: \t//\n314: \t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\n315: \t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\n316: \t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\n317: \t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\n318: \t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\n319: \t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\n320: \t//\n321: \t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\n322: \t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\n323: \t// problem:\n324: \t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\n325: \t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\n326: \t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\n327: \t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\n328: \t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\n329: \t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\n330: \t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\n331: \t//\n332: \t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\n333: \t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\n334: \t// hitting the \"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\n335: \t// for disjoint sets of keys\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\n336: \tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\n337: }\n338: \n339: // New initializes a new plugin and returns it.\n340: func New(ctx context.Context, plArgs runtime.Object, fh framework.Handle, fts feature.Features) (framework.Plugin, error) {\n341: \tif !fts.EnableDynamicResourceAllocation {\n342: Entry point where event handlers are registered via `addAllEventHandlers()`\n\n2. **Called from**: `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (line 287)\n   - Function iterates over `gvkMap` and registers event handlers for each GVK\n   - Returns list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that should trigger re-queuing\n   - **BUG**: ResourceSlice is NOT in this list\n\n5. **Plugin uses resourceSliceLister in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` to fetch available resources\n   - `newResourceModel()` in `structuredparameters.go` (line 51) lists all ResourceSlices\n\n6. **GVK constant missing from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 68-106)\n   - Lists all framework.GVK constants but ResourceSlice is missing\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**There are TWO root causes that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-queuing:**\n\n### Root Cause #1: Missing GVK Constant Definition\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Location**: Lines 68-106 (const block for GVK definitions)\n- **Line**: After line 96 (ResourceClassParameters constant)\n- **Explanation**: The `framework.ResourceSlice` GVK constant is not defined, making it impossible to reference ResourceSlice in event registration code\n\n### Root Cause #2: Missing Event Registration in DynamicResources Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~412 (end of events slice definition)\n- **Explanation**: The `EventsToRegister()` method returns a list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that declare which events should trigger pod re-queuing. ResourceSlice events (Add/Update) are missing from this list, even though the plugin uses `resourceSliceLister` to fetch ResourceSlice data during the Filter phase (line 958).\n\n## Why This Causes the Bug\n\nWhen a pod requests DRA resources:\n\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler before ResourceSlices exist\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter/PreScore phase tries to allocate resources\n3. `newResourceModel()` is called, which lists all ResourceSlices (line 51 of structuredparameters.go)\n4. Since no ResourceSlices exist, the filter fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n5. Pod is added to the unschedulable queue\n6. **Later, when the DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices:**\n   - ResourceSlice Add/Update events are generated\n   - BUT: ResourceSlice events are NOT registered in eventhandlers.go (because they're not in the GVK map)\n   - Pod in unschedulable queue is **NEVER re-evaluated**\n   - Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\nThe race condition: if the driver starts FIRST, ResourceSlices exist before the pod arrives, so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives first, it gets stuck because resource availability changes don't trigger re-queuing.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: In the GVK constants block (after line 96)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix #2: Register ResourceSlice Events in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n**Location**: In the events slice (after line 410, before the closing `]`)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices provide information about available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### Fix #3: Add Event Handler for ResourceSlice (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n**Location**: In the switch/case block (after line 474, in the ResourceClassParameters case, before the closing utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n## Analysis: Detailed Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n### Phase 1: Scheduler Initialization\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` initializes the scheduler\n2. It calls plugins to get their `EventsToRegister()` at line ~300s\n3. `DynamicResourceAllocation` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` is called (dynamicresources.go:381)\n4. The plugin returns a slice of ClusterEventWithHint that includes:\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add, Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add, Update)\n   - Node (Add, UpdateNodeLabel, UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add, Update)\n   - **MISSING: ResourceSlice (Add, Update)**\n\n5. `unionedGVKs()` is called (scheduler.go:525) to collect all GVKs from all plugins\n6. Since ResourceSlice is not in EventsToRegister(), it's not in the gvkMap\n7. `addAllEventHandlers()` is called with this incomplete gvkMap\n8. DynamicResources plugin's PreFilter phase initializes the state\n5. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls:\n   - `newResourceModel()` (line 958) which lists all ResourceSlices\n   - Since ResourceSlices don't exist yet, allocation fails\n   - Filter returns Unschedulable\n\n6. Pod is moved to unschedulable queue via SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n7. Pod waits for one of its registered events to occur\n\n### Phase 3: Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlices (BUG MANIFESTS)\n\n1. DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects\n2. Kubernetes API server generates ResourceSlice Add/Update events\n3. Informer receives these events and calls registered event handlers\n4. **BUT: No event handler is registered for ResourceSlice** (because it wasn't in gvkMap)\n5. Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n\n### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n\nIf ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls `newResourceModel()`\n3. ResourceSlices are listed successfully\n4. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n5. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n",

Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n",
  "filePath": "/logs/agent/solution.md",
  "originalFile": null,
  "structuredPatch": [],
  "type": "create"
}

  "originalFile": "# Bug Investigation: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go** \u2014 examined to find framework.GVK constant definitions\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go** \u2014 examined for EventsToRegister() method that declares which cluster events should trigger pod re-queuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** \u2014 examined for addAllEventHandlers() which registers informer event handlers based on plugin-declared GVKs\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** \u2014 examined for the initialization path that connects event handlers to the scheduling queue\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go** \u2014 examined to see how resourceSliceLister is used\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (~line 358)\n   - Entry point where event handlers are registered via `addAllEventHandlers()`\n\n2. **Called from**: `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (line 287)\n   - Function iterates over `gvkMap` and registers event handlers for each GVK\n   - `gvkMap` is built from `unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile)`\n\n3. **GVK map populated by**: `unionedGVKs()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (line 525)\n   - Collects GVKs from all plugins' `EventsToRegister()` methods\n\n4. **Plugin declares events via**: `EventsToRegister()` in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 381)\n   - Returns list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that should trigger re-queuing\n   - **BUG**: ResourceSlice is NOT in this list\n\n5. **Plugin uses resourceSliceLister in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` to fetch available resources\n   - `newResourceModel()` in `structuredparameters.go` (line 51) lists all ResourceSlices\n\n6. **GVK constant missing from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 68-106)\n   - Lists all framework.GVK constants but ResourceSlice is missing\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**There are TWO root causes that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-queuing:**\n\n### Root Cause #1: Missing GVK Constant Definition\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Location**: Lines 68-106 (const block for GVK definitions)\n- **Line**: After line 96 (ResourceClassParameters constant)\n- **Explanation**: The `framework.ResourceSlice` GVK constant is not defined, making it impossible to reference ResourceSlice in event registration code\n\n### Root Cause #2: Missing Event Registration in DynamicResources Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~412 (end of events slice definition)\n- **Explanation**: The `EventsToRegister()` method returns a list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that declare which events should trigger pod re-queuing. ResourceSlice events (Add/Update) are missing from this list, even though the plugin uses `resourceSliceLister` to fetch ResourceSlice data during the Filter phase (line 958).\n\n## Why This Causes the Bug\n\nWhen a pod requests DRA resources:\n\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler before ResourceSlices exist\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter/PreScore phase tries to allocate resources\n3. `newResourceModel()` is called, which lists all ResourceSlices (line 51 of structuredparameters.go)\n4. Since no ResourceSlices exist, the filter fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n5. Pod is added to the unschedulable queue\n6. **Later, when the DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices:**\n   - ResourceSlice Add/Update events are generated\n   - BUT: ResourceSlice events are NOT registered in eventhandlers.go (because they're not in the GVK map)\n   - Pod in unschedulable queue is **NEVER re-evaluated**\n   - Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\nThe race condition: if the driver starts FIRST, ResourceSlices exist before the pod arrives, so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives first, it gets stuck because resource availability changes don't trigger re-queuing.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: In the GVK constants block (after line 96)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix #2: Register ResourceSlice Events in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n**Location**: In the events slice (after line 410, before the closing `]`)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices provide information about available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### Fix #3: Add Event Handler for ResourceSlice (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n**Location**: In the switch/case block (after line 474, in the ResourceClassParameters case, before the closing `}`)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n## Analysis: Detailed Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n### Phase 1: Scheduler Initialization\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` initializes the scheduler\n2. It calls plugins to get their `EventsToRegister()` at line ~300s\n3. `DynamicResourceAllocation` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` is called (dynamicresources.go:381)\n4. The plugin returns a slice of ClusterEventWithHint that includes:\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add, Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add, Update)\n   - Node (Add, UpdateNodeLabel, UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add, Update)\n   - **MISSING: ResourceSlice (Add, Update)**\n\n5. `unionedGVKs()` is called (scheduler.go:525) to collect all GVKs from all plugins\n6. Since ResourceSlice is not in EventsToRegister(), it's not in the gvkMap\n7. `addAllEventHandlers()` is called with this incomplete gvkMap\n8. The function iterates over gvkMap and registers event handlers\n9. **ResourceSlice case is never hit because ResourceSlice GVK is not in gvkMap**\n\n### Phase 2: Pod Scheduling (Pod Arrives Before Driver)\n\n1. Pod with DRA ResourceClaims arrives at scheduler\n2. Pod is added to scheduling queue via `addPodToSchedulingQueue()` (line 125)\n3. Scheduler attempts to schedule the pod\n4. DynamicResources plugin's PreFilter phase initializes the state\n5. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls:\n   - `newResourceModel()` (line 958) which lists all ResourceSlices\n   - Since ResourceSlices don't exist yet, allocation fails\n   - Filter returns Unschedulable\n\n6. Pod is moved to unschedulable queue via SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n7. Pod waits for one of its registered events to occur\n\n### Phase 3: Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlices (BUG MANIFESTS)\n\n1. DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects\n2. Kubernetes API server generates ResourceSlice Add/Update events\n3. Informer receives these events and calls registered event handlers\n4. **BUT: No event handler is registered for ResourceSlice** (because it wasn't in gvkMap)\n5. Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n\n### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n\nIf ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls `newResourceModel()`\n3. ResourceSlices are listed successfully\n4. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n5. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n",

Pod is added to the unschedulable queue\n6. **Later, when the DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices:**\n   - ResourceSlice Add/Update events are generated\n   - BUT: ResourceSlice events are NOT registered in eventhandlers.go (because they're not in the GVK map)\n   - Pod in unschedulable queue is **NEVER re-evaluated**\n   - Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\nThe race condition: if the driver starts FIRST, ResourceSlices exist before the pod arrives, so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives first, it gets stuck because resource availability changes don't trigger re-queuing.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Lines**: After line 96 (ResourceClassParameters constant) and before line 97 (blank line)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix #2: Register ResourceSlice Events in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n**Lines**: After line 410 (ResourceClass event) and before line 411 (closing `]`)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices provide information about available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### Fix #3: Add Event Handler for ResourceSlice\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n**Location**: In the switch/case statement for gvkMap\n**Lines**: After line 492 (end of ResourceClassParameters case) and before line 493 (StorageClass case)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n**Why all three fixes are necessary:**\n1. **GVK Constant** enables referencing ResourceSlice in code throughout the framework\n2. **Event Registration in Plugin** declares to the scheduler that ResourceSlice events matter to the DynamicResources plugin\n3. **Event Handler** connects the informer callback to the scheduling queue so unschedulable pods can be re-queued when ResourceSlices change\n\n## Analysis: Detailed Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n### Phase 1: Scheduler Initialization\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` initializes the scheduler\n2. It calls plugins to get their `EventsToRegister()` at line ~300s\n3. `DynamicResourceAllocation` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` is called (dynamicresources.go:381)\n4. The plugin returns a slice of ClusterEventWithHint that includes:\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add, Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add, Update)\n   - Node (Add, UpdateNodeLabel, UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add, Update)\n   - **MISSING: ResourceSlice (Add, Update)**\n\n5. `unionedGVKs()` is called (scheduler.go:525) to collect all GVKs from all plugins\n6. Since ResourceSlice is not in EventsToRegister(), it's not in the gvkMap\n7. `addAllEventHandlers()` is called with this incomplete gvkMap\n8. The function iterates over gvkMap and registers event handlers\n9. **ResourceSlice case is never hit because ResourceSlice GVK is not in gvkMap**\n\n### Phase 2: Pod Scheduling (Pod Arrives Before Driver)\n\n1. Pod with DRA ResourceClaims arrives at scheduler\n2. Pod is added to scheduling queue via `addPodToSchedulingQueue()` (line 125)\n3. Scheduler attempts to schedule the pod\n4. DynamicResources plugin's PreFilter phase initializes the state\n5. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls:\n   - `newResourceModel()` (line 958) which lists all ResourceSlices\n   - Since ResourceSlices don't exist yet, allocation fails\n   - Filter returns Unschedulable\n\n6. Pod is moved to unschedulable queue via SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n7. Pod waits for one of its registered events to occur\n\n### Phase 3: Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlices (BUG MANIFESTS)\n\n1. DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects\n2. Kubernetes API server generates ResourceSlice Add/Update events\n3. Informer receives these events and calls registered event handlers\n4. **BUT: No event handler is registered for ResourceSlice** (because it wasn't in gvkMap)\n5. Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n\n### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n\nIf ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls `newResourceModel()`\n3. ResourceSlices are listed successfully\n4. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n5. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n",

# Bug Investigation: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Files Examined

- **pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go** — examined to find framework.GVK constant definitions
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go** — examined for EventsToRegister() method that declares which cluster events should trigger pod re-queuing
- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — examined for addAllEventHandlers() which registers informer event handlers based on plugin-declared GVKs
- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — examined for the initialization path that connects event handlers to the scheduling queue
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go** — examined to see how resourceSliceLister is used

## Dependency Chain

1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (~line 358)
   - Entry point where event handlers are registered via `addAllEventHandlers()`

2. **Called from**: `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (line 287)
   - Function iterates over `gvkMap` and registers event handlers for each GVK
   - `gvkMap` is built from `unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile)`

3. **GVK map populated by**: `unionedGVKs()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (line 525)
   - Collects GVKs from all plugins' `EventsToRegister()` methods

4. **Plugin declares events via**: `EventsToRegister()` in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 381)
   - Returns list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that should trigger re-queuing
   - **BUG**: ResourceSlice is NOT in this list

5. **Plugin uses resourceSliceLister in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 958)
   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ..

## Proposed Fix

### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant

**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
**Location**: In the GVK constants block (after line 96)

```diff
 	ResourceClaim           GVK = "ResourceClaim"
 	ResourceClass           GVK = "ResourceClass"
 	ResourceClaimParameters GVK = "ResourceClaimParameters"
 	ResourceClassParameters GVK = "ResourceClassParameters"
+	ResourceSlice           GVK = "ResourceSlice"

 	// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.
```

**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`
**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`

+		// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.
+		{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},
 	}
 	return events
```
